Z","content":"Those percentages represent **Feature Importances** from the Machine Learning (Random Forest) model. 
\n\nEssentially, the AI analyzed all historical dropouts and calculated *which specific data points are the strongest 
predictors* that a patient is about to quit therapy. The higher the percentage, the more heavily the AI weighs that 
factor when calculating dropout risk.\n\nHere is what each one means:\n\n1. **`srs_relationship` (21.6%)**: The 
strongest predictor of dropout is the \"Relationship\" score on the Session Rating Scale. If a patient feels unheard, 
disrespected, or disconnected from their therapist, they are extremely likely to leave.\n2. **`srs_overall` (21.1%)**: 
The patient's general rating of the session as a whole. A consistently low overall score is a massive red flag for 
impending dropout.\n3. **`srs_goals` (16.1%)**: How well the session aligned with what the patient *wanted* to work 
on. If the therapist pushes their own agenda and ignores the patient's goals, dropout risk spikes.\n4. 
**`srs_approach` (12.6%)**: How well the therapist's methodology fits the patient (e.g., CBT vs. psychoanalysis). A 
mismatch here drives 12.6% of the AI's dropout predictions.\n5. **`srs_drop` (12.0%)**: This isn't a raw score, but 
the *momentum* or *change* between sessions. If a patient's score goes from an 8.0 down to a 5.0 (a 3.0 point drop), 
that sudden downward trend is a huge warning sign.\n6. **`no_shows` (5.5%)**: The number of appointments the patient 
has missed. While skipping an appointment is a bad sign, the AI learned that the *Session Rating Scale scores* (the 
emotional connection) are actually 4x more predictive of a dropout than just missing a meeting!\n7. **`age` (~5%)**: 
Demographics play a small role. The AI has found that younger patients (under 25) historically have slightly higher 
volatility and dropout rates than older patients.","thinking":"**Prioritizing Tool Usage**\n\nI'm now focusing on tool
